This skill handles **execution only** for STANDARD and STRICT tier tasks.\n>\n> If for any reason no classification header was emitted before this skill was invoked, emit one now using ONLY the tier values STRICT, STANDARD, LIGHT, or EXEMPT (no other values are valid).\n\n# /sc:task-unified - Unified Task Execution with Compliance\n\n## Purpose\n\nUnified command that merges orchestration capabilities with MCP compliance enforcement. Automatically classifies tasks into compliance tiers and enforces appropriate verification.\n\n**Key Benefits**:\n- Single command replaces confusion between `sc:task` and `sc:task-mcp`\n- Automatic tier classification with confidence scoring\n- Appropriate verification for each task type\n- Prevents over-engineering for trivial changes\n- Ensures safety for critical changes\n\n## Triggers\n\nUse `/sc:task` when:\n- Task involves code modifications with downstream impacts\n- Complexity score >0.6 with code modifications\n- Multi-file scope (>2 estimated affected files)\n- Security domain paths detected (auth/, security/, crypto/)\n- Refactoring or system-wide changes requested\n\n**Auto-Suggest Keywords**:\n- High confidence: \"implement feature\", \"refactor system\", \"fix security\", \"add authentication\", \"update database schema\"\n- Moderate confidence: \"add new\", \"create component\", \"update service\", \"modify API\"\n\n## Usage\n\n```bash\n/sc:task [description]                           # Auto-detect all dimensions\n/sc:task [description] --compliance strict       # Force STRICT tier\n/sc:task [description] --compliance light        # Force LIGHT tier\n/sc:task [description] --skip-compliance         # Bypass compliance (escape hatch)\n/sc:task [description] --verify auto             # Auto-select verification\n```\n\n## Behavioral Flow\n\n### 0. Classification (Already Performed)\n\nClassification was handled by the `/sc:task` command before this skill was invoked. The tier has been determined and the classification header has been emitted. Proceed directly to execution based on the classified tier.\n\n**Reference** ŌĆö the tier keyword tables (for context only, do not re-classify):\n- **STRICT**: security, authentication, database, migration, refactor, breaking change, encrypt, token, session, oauth\n- **EXEMPT**: explain, search, commit, push, plan, discuss, brainstorm\n- **LIGHT**: typo, comment, whitespace, lint, docstring, formatting, minor\n- **STANDARD**: implement, add, create, update, fix, build, modify, change (default)\n\n### 2. Confidence Display (Human-Readable)\n\nAfter the mandatory classification header, show a human-readable summary:\n\n```\n**Tier: STANDARD** [Ō¢łŌ¢łŌ¢łŌ¢łŌ¢łŌ¢łŌ¢łŌ¢łŌ¢æŌ¢æ] 80%\n\nClassified as STANDARD:\n- Keywords matched: add, implement\n- Confidence score: 0.78\n- Considered alternatives: STRICT (0.35)\n```\n\nIf confidence <70%, add prompt: \"ŌÜĀ’ĖÅ Low confidence. Override with: `--compliance [strict|standard|light|exempt]`\"\n\n**Note**: The machine-readable header (Section 0) is for telemetry/A/B testing. This human-readable display is for user understanding.\n\n### 3. Execution Phase\n\nExecute task according to tier requirements:\n\n**STRICT Execution**:\n1. Activate project (mcp__serena__activate_project)\n2. Verify git working directory clean (git status)\n3. Load codebase context (codebase-retrieval)\n4. Check relevant memories (list_memories -> read_memory)\n5. Identify all affected files and test files\n6. Make changes with full checklist\n7. Identify all files that import changed code\n8. Update all affected files\n9. Spawn verification agent (quality-engineer)\n10. Run comprehensive tests: `pytest [path] -v`\n11. Answer adversarial questions\n\n**STANDARD Execution**:\n1. Load context via codebase-retrieval\n2. Search downstream impacts (find_referencing_symbols OR grep)\n3. Make changes\n4. Run affected tests OR document manual verification\n5. Verify basic functionality\n\n**LIGHT Execution**:\n1. Quick scope check (files/lines within bounds)\n2. Make changes\n3. Quick sanity check (syntax valid, no obvious errors)\n4. Proceed with judgment\n\n**EXEMPT Execution**:\n1. Execute immediately\n2. No verification overhead\n\n### 4. Verification Phase\n\nRoute to appropriate verification based on tier and paths:\n\n| Compliance Tier | Verification Method | Token Cost | Timeout |\n|-----------------|---------------------|------------|---------|\n| STRICT | Sub-agent (quality-engineer) | 3-5K | 60s |\n| STANDARD | Direct test execution | 300-500 | 30s |\n| LIGHT | Skip verification | 0 | 0s |\n| EXEMPT | Skip verification | 0 | 0s |\n\n**Critical Path Override**: Paths matching `auth/`, `security/`, `crypto/`, `models/`, `migrations/` always trigger CRITICAL verification regardless of compliance tier.\n\n**Trivial Path Override**: Paths matching `*.md`, `docs/`, `*test*.py` may skip verification.\n\n### 4.5 Test Failure Escalation Protocol (TFEP)\n\n**CRITICAL**: When tests fail during the Verification Phase (Section 4), agents MUST follow this protocol. Ad-hoc fixes are PROHIBITED.\n\n#### TFEP Prohibition Rules (VIOLATION-level)\n\nThese rules apply to ALL compliance tiers that run tests (STRICT, STANDARD):\n\n1. **VIOLATION**: Agents MUST NOT fix any code in response to test failures without completing the TFEP workflow.\n2. **VIOLATION**: Agents MUST NOT modify test expectations to make failing tests pass without adversarial validation.\n3. **VIOLATION**: Ad-hoc patches derived from test output are PROHIBITED. The agent must not read a traceback and immediately edit code to resolve it.\n\n**Permitted Exceptions** (MAY fix directly without TFEP):\n- Single `ImportError`/`NameError` in test scaffolding the agent just wrote, affecting <=2 tests, where the error is in the test file itself (not in implementation code).\n- Lint/formatting failures (trivially fixable, unambiguous root cause).\n- Deprecation warnings (not failures).\n\n**Valid Adversarial Outcome**: \"Test expectations are wrong\" is a legitimate conclusion from adversarial debate. When the debate concludes that test expectations are outdated rather than the code being wrong, this is NOT grounds for the agent to directly edit the tests ŌĆö it must be presented to the user for review.\n\n#### Test Baseline Snapshot (Pre-Implementation)\n\nBefore implementation begins, the agent MUST record a test baseline:\n\n1. Capture the list of all existing test files and test function names at task start (e.g., via `uv run pytest --collect-only -q` or directory listing).\n2. Store this baseline in memory for the duration of the task.\n3. On any test failure, classify each failing test as:\n   - **Pre-existing**: Test name appears in the baseline (existed before this task).\n   - **New**: Test name does NOT appear in the baseline (written by the agent during this task).\n4. This classification drives the MUST-escalate vs MAY-fix-directly decision below.\n\n#### Escalation Trigger Detection\n\n**MUST escalate (trigger TFEP):**\n- Any **pre-existing test** fails (tests in the baseline that were not modified by the agent). This is the primary trigger ŌĆö regressions in existing tests indicate the implementation broke something.\n- **3 or more new tests** fail simultaneously (indicates a systemic issue, not a simple typo).\n- **Runtime exceptions in implementation code** (TypeError, AttributeError, KeyError, etc. in the code being tested, not in the test scaffolding itself).\n\n**Escalation gradient (within-TFEP, for future forensic integration):**\n- Repeated failure (same test cluster fails after fix attempt) ŌåÆ escalate from light to standard\n- Multi-file blast radius from recent changes ŌåÆ escalate\n- Low-confidence root cause from adversarial debate ŌåÆ escalate\n- Unresolved adversarial outcome (no winner/tie) ŌåÆ escalate\n- Second failed retest ŌåÆ escalate\n- Cross-domain or non-obvious regression ŌåÆ escalate\n\n#### TFEP Execution Flow\n\nWhen TFEP triggers, execute the following steps:\n\n**Step 1: Halt and freeze**\n1. **STOP** testing immediately.\n2. **FREEZE** implementation ŌĆö no further code changes permitted.\n\n**Step 2: Construct failure context**\n3. Build a `failure_context` YAML package containing:\n   - `test_names`: list of failing test function names\n   - `test_files`: list of test files containing failures\n   - `error_output`: full traceback/error output\n   - `expected_behavior`: what was expected\n   - `actual_behavior`: what actually happened\n   - `changes_made`: files changed during this task with descriptions\n   - `task_description`: current task description\n   - `test_baseline`: the pre-implementation test baseline\n   - `escalation_count`: which TFEP trigger this is (1, 2, or 3)\n4. Write context to `{output_dir}/context.yaml`.\n\n**Step 3: Invoke forensic**\n5. Determine the forensic tier based on escalation count:\n   - 1st trigger ŌåÆ `--tier light --intent triage`\n   - 2nd trigger ŌåÆ `--tier standard`\n   - 3rd trigger ŌåÆ **FULL STOP**. Report to user. Do not attempt further fixes.\n6. Invoke: `/sc:forensic --tier {tier} --intent triage --caller task-unified --context {context_path} --output {output_dir} --depth quick`\n7. The forensic pipeline runs autonomously through all its phases and returns a structured return contract.\n\n**Step 4: Consume forensic results**\n8. Read the forensic return contract from `{output_dir}/return-contract.yaml`.\n9. Handle based on status:\n   - If `test_is_wrong == true`: Present to user for review. Do NOT auto-fix tests.\n   - If `status == \"success\"`: Proceed to Step 5 (tasklist insertion).\n   - If `status == \"partial\"` or `recommended_escalation != \"none\"`: Increment `escalation_count` and return to Step 3.\n   - If `status == \"failed\"`: Report to user, halt execution.\n\n**Step 5: Tasklist insertion**\n10. Read `tasklist_insertion_path` from the return contract.\n11. Insert the remediation block into the current tasklist:\n    - Add `## Failure Remediation Plan (Adjudicated)` heading.\n    - Insert remediation tasks BEFORE existing test/verification tasks.\n    - Preserve original tasklist structure ŌĆö append, don't replace.\n\n**Step 6: Resume**\n12. Resume execution with `--compliance strict` starting from the inserted remediation tasks.\n13. After remediation tasks complete, re-run the original test suite.\n14. If tests pass: TFEP resolved successfully. Produce incident report and continue.\n15. If tests fail again: Increment `escalation_count`, return to Step 2.\n\n#### TFEP Incident Reporting\n\nAfter each TFEP resolution (success or escalation), produce `tfep-incident-report.md`:\n\n```markdown\n# TFEP Incident Report\n\n- **Trigger**: {which threshold rule fired}\n- **Escalation count**: {1, 2, or 3}\n- **Failing tests**: {test names and classification}\n- **Root cause**: {summary from rca-verdict.md}\n- **Solution**: {summary from solution-verdict.md}\n- **Outcome**: {success / escalated / failed}\n- **Forensic artifacts**: {path to output_dir}\n```\n\nThis report is committed to git alongside other forensic artifacts.\n\n#### Escalation Budget\n\n```\n1st TFEP trigger  ŌåÆ /sc:forensic --tier light --intent triage    (~5-8K tokens)\n2nd TFEP trigger  ŌåÆ /sc:forensic --tier standard                 (~15-20K tokens)\n3rd TFEP trigger  ŌåÆ FULL STOP. Report to user. Do not attempt further fixes.\n```\n\n### 5. Four pure-Python detection modules ŌĆö obligation scanner, integration contract extractor, fingerprint coverage checker, and spec structural auditor ŌĆö catch the class of \"scaffold-without-discharge\" bugs that LLM-on-LLM review structurally misses. The gate slots between `merge` and `test-strategy` in the existing pipeline, is additive-only to shared files, and ships with `gate_rollout_mode=off`, where the gate still evaluates but the result is ignored until shadow validation confirms accuracy.\n    12ŌåÆ\n    13ŌåÆ**Scope**: 35 functional requirements (FR-MOD1ŌĆō4, FR-GATE, FR-EXEC, FR-PROMPT, FR-SPRINT) and 10 non-functional requirements (NFR-001ŌĆō011, excluding NFR-003) across 12 new files and 5 modified files (~1,200 LOC). HIGH complexity (0.72) driven by dual execution context (standalone roadmap vs sprint-invoked) and three independent regex engines.\n    14ŌåÆ\n    15ŌåÆ**Key architectural decisions**:\n    16ŌåÆ- All detection is deterministic Python. No LLM calls. Non-negotiable per NFR-001.\n    17ŌåÆ- `off` means gate fires but result is not submitted to sprint infrastructure (backward-compatible). Shadow mode adds metrics recording.\n    18ŌåÆ- D-03/D-04 coexistence: defense-in-depth (both gates evaluate independently per NFR-010).\n    19ŌåÆ- Prompt changes are probability reducers, not enforcement. Deterministic checks are authoritative.\n    20ŌåÆ\n    21ŌåÆ**Delivery structure**: 4 build phases with 3 explicit validation checkpoints (A: implementation readiness, B: rollout readiness, C: enforcement readiness). 170ŌåÆ| Mode | Gate Evaluation | Metrics Recording | Task Behavior |\n   171ŌåÆ|------|----------------|-------------------|---------------|\n   172ŌåÆ| `off` | Yes (result ignored) | None | No change |\n   173ŌåÆ| `shadow` | Yes | `ShadowGateMetrics.record()` | No change |\n   174ŌåÆ| `soft` | Yes | `ShadowGateMetrics.record()` | Credit on pass; remediation + `BUDGET_EXHAUSTED` on fail |\n Four pure-Python detection modules ŌĆö obligation scanner, integration contract extractor, fingerprint coverage checker, and spec structural auditor ŌĆö catch the class of \"scaffold-without-discharge\" bugs that LLM-on-LLM review structurally misses. The gate slots between `merge` and `test-strategy` in the existing pipeline, is additive-only to shared files, and ships with `gate_rollout_mode=off`, where the gate still evaluates but the result is ignored until shadow validation confirms accuracy.\n    12ŌåÆ\n    13ŌåÆ**Scope**: 35 functional requirements (FR-MOD1ŌĆō4, FR-GATE, FR-EXEC, FR-PROMPT, FR-SPRINT) and 10 non-functional requirements (NFR-001ŌĆō011, excluding NFR-003) across 12 new files and 5 modified files (~1,200 LOC). No LLM calls. Non-negotiable per NFR-001.\n    17ŌåÆ- `off` means gate fires but result is not submitted to sprint infrastructure (backward-compatible). Problem Statement\n    17ŌåÆ\n    18ŌåÆ<!-- Source: Merge (new content bridging V2+V5) -->\n    19ŌåÆ\n    20ŌåÆLLMs exhibit several correlated tendencies when generating multi-phase roadmaps from specifications. These tendencies cause systematic omission of integration wiring, undischarged scaffolding obligations, and dropped code-level requirements -- even when the output passes all existing format and fidelity gates.\n    21ŌåÆ\n    22ŌåÆThe Anti-Instincts Gate is a unified deterministic defense layer that addresses four failure modes simultaneously:\n    23ŌåÆ\n    24ŌåÆ| Failure Mode | Detection Module | Source |\n    25ŌåÆ|---|---|---|\n    26ŌåÆ| Undischarged scaffolding (mocks/stubs never replaced) | `obligation_scanner.py` | V2-A |\n    27ŌåÆ| Missing integration wiring (dispatch tables, registries never populated) | `integration_contracts.py` | V5-1 |\n    28ŌåÆ| Code-level identifier omissions (function names, constants dropped) | `fingerprint.py` | V4-2 |\n    29ŌåÆ| Extraction-stage requirement loss (upstream guard) | `spec_structural_audit.py` | V1-C |\n    30ŌåÆ\n    31ŌåÆAdditionally, a prompt-level prevention layer reduces generation-time omissions:\n    32ŌåÆ\n    33ŌåÆ| Prevention Layer | Target | Source |\n    34ŌåÆ|---|---|---|\n    35ŌåÆ| Integration enumeration block in generate prompt | `prompts.py` | V1-D + V5-2 |\n    36ŌåÆ| Integration wiring dimension in spec-fidelity prompt | `prompts.py` | V5-2 |\n    37ŌåÆ\n    38ŌåÆ---\n    39ŌåÆ\n    40ŌåÆ## 2. Evidence: The cli-portify Bug\n    41ŌåÆ\n    42ŌåÆ<!-- Source: Merge (new content bridging V2+V5) -->\n    43ŌåÆ\n    44ŌåÆ### What the spec defined\n    45ŌåÆ\n    46ŌåÆThree release specs (v2.24, v2.24.1, v2.25) specified:\n    47ŌåÆ\n    48ŌåÆ- **Three-way dispatch**: `_run_programmatic_step()`, `_run_claude_step()`, `_run_convergence_step()`\n    49ŌåÆ- **`PROGRAMMATIC_RUNNERS` dictionary**: Maps step IDs to Python functions\n    50ŌåÆ- **Module dependency graph**: `executor.py --> steps/validate_config.py`, etc.\n    51ŌåÆ- **Integration test**: `test_programmatic_step_routing`\n    52ŌåÆ\n    53ŌåÆ### What the roadmap produced\n    54ŌåÆ\n    55ŌåÆThe roadmap reduced the executor to: \"Implement executor: sequential execution only, `--dry-run`, `--resume <step-id>`, signal handling\" with milestone M2: \"Sequential pipeline runs end-to-end with **mocked steps**.\"\n    56ŌåÆ\n    57ŌåÆZero mentions of `PROGRAMMATIC_RUNNERS`, three-way dispatch, or the `executor.py --> steps/*.py` import chain.\n    58ŌåÆ\n    59ŌåÆ### How existing gates failed\n    60ŌåÆ\n    61ŌåÆThe `SPEC_FIDELITY_GATE` enforces `high_severity_count == 0` deterministically, but the LLM generating the severity counts shared the same blindspot as the generator. The deterministic enforcement was sound; the LLM input to that gate was wrong.\n    62ŌåÆ\n    63ŌåÆ### How each module in this spec would have caught it\n    64ŌåÆ\n    65ŌåÆ| Module | Detection mechanism | Confidence |\n    66ŌåÆ|---|---|---|\n    67ŌåÆ| `obligation_scanner.py` | \"mocked steps\" in Phase 2 with no discharge in later phases | 85% |\n    68ŌåÆ| `integration_contracts.py` | `PROGRAMMATIC_RUNNERS` dispatch pattern with no wiring task | 90% |\n    69ŌåÆ| `fingerprint.py` | `_run_programmatic_step`, `PROGRAMMATIC_RUNNERS`, `test_programmatic_step_routing` absent from roadmap | 95% |\n    70ŌåÆ| `spec_structural_audit.py` | Pseudocode block + `PROGRAMMATIC_RUNNERS` registry + `def _run_*` signatures inflate structural count beyond extraction's requirement count | 85% |\n    71ŌåÆ\n    72ŌåÆ---\n    73ŌåÆ\n    74ŌåÆ## 3. Architecture\n    75ŌåÆ\n    76ŌåÆ<!-- Source: Merge (new content bridging V2+V5) -->\n    77ŌåÆ\n    78ŌåÆ```\n    79ŌåÆSpec ŌöĆŌöĆ[V1-C: Structural audit]ŌöĆŌöĆ> Extraction validated\n    80ŌåÆ                                         |\n    81ŌåÆ                                    [V1-D+V5-2: Prompt constraint]\n    82ŌåÆ                                         |\n    83ŌåÆ                              LLM generates roadmap\n    84ŌåÆ                                         |\n    85ŌåÆ                                    Merge step\n    86ŌåÆ                                         |\n    87ŌåÆ                          +--------------+--------------+\n    88ŌåÆ                          |              |              |\n    89ŌåÆ                    [V2-A: Obligation    [V5-1: Contract   [V4-2: Fingerprint\n    90ŌåÆ                     scanner]            extractor]         coverage]\n    91ŌåÆ                          |              |              |\n    92ŌåÆ                          +--------------+--------------+\n    93ŌåÆ                                         |\n    94ŌåÆ                              ANTI_INSTINCT_GATE (STRICT)\n    95ŌåÆ                                         |\n    96ŌåÆ                                    GATE FAIL / Proceed to spec-fidelity\n    97ŌåÆ```\n    98ŌåÆ\n    99ŌåÆ**Pipeline position**: The three post-merge checks run as a single non-LLM step between `merge` and `test-strategy` in the pipeline. The structural audit runs between `extract` and `generate` as an executor-level hook.\n   100ŌåÆ\n   101ŌåÆ**Key design property**: All four detection modules are pure Python with zero LLM calls. This is deliberate -- LLM-on-LLM review shares the same blindspots that caused the original bug. The deterministic floor cannot be bypassed by completion bias.\n   102ŌåÆ\n   103ŌåÆ**Dual execution context**: When the roadmap pipeline executes within a sprint task context, gate results propagate to the sprint-level `TrailingGateRunner` and `TurnLedger` for economic tracking. In standalone mode, gate evaluation is synchronous pass/fail with no budget interaction. See Sections 9.5 and 16.5 for details.\n   104ŌåÆ\n   105ŌåÆ---\n   106ŌåÆ\n   107ŌåÆ## 4. Module 1: Obligation Scanner\n   108ŌåÆ\n   109ŌåÆ<!-- Source: V2-A (obligation scanner) -->\n   110ŌåÆ\n   111ŌåÆ### Concept\n   112ŌåÆ\n   113ŌåÆA deterministic, regex-based post-generation pass that scans the merged roadmap for scaffolding terms and verifies each has a corresponding discharge task in a later phase. Catches the failure mode where early phases use \"mocked\", \"stub\", \"skeleton\", \"placeholder\" language that creates implicit obligations that later phases never fulfill.\n   114ŌåÆ\n   115ŌåÆ### Detection Axis\n   116ŌåÆ\n   117ŌåÆV2-A's obligation scanner detects a fundamentally different failure mode than omission-based approaches. Rather than checking whether a requirement is present, it checks whether deferred commitments are fulfilled. This catches bugs where the requirement IS mentioned (as scaffolding) but the follow-through is missing.\n   118ŌåÆ\n   119ŌåÆ### Implementation\n   120ŌåÆ\n   121ŌåÆ**File**: `src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/obligation_scanner.py` (new, ~200 LOC)\n   122ŌåÆ\n   123ŌåÆ```python\n   124ŌåÆ\"\"\"Obligation scanner -- detects undischarged scaffolding obligations in roadmaps.\n   125ŌåÆ\n   126ŌåÆScans roadmap content for scaffolding terms (mock, stub, skeleton, placeholder,\n   127ŌåÆscaffold, temporary, hardcoded) that create implicit obligations, then verifies\n   128ŌåÆeach obligation has a corresponding discharge term (replace, wire, integrate,\n   129ŌåÆconnect, implement real, remove mock, swap) in a later phase.\n   130ŌåÆ\n   131ŌåÆPure function: content in, findings out. No I/O.\n   132ŌåÆ\"\"\"\n   133ŌåÆ\n   134ŌåÆfrom __future__ import annotations\n   135ŌåÆ\n   136ŌåÆimport re\n   137ŌåÆfrom dataclasses import dataclass\n   138ŌåÆ\n   139ŌåÆ\n   140ŌåÆ# --- Obligation vocabulary ---\n   141ŌåÆ\n   142ŌåÆ# Terms that CREATE an obligation (something deferred)\n   143ŌåÆSCAFFOLD_TERMS = [\n   144ŌåÆ    r\"\\bmocked?\\b\",\n   145ŌåÆ    r\"\\bstub(?:bed|s)?\\b\",\n   146ŌåÆ    r\"\\bskeleton\\b\",\n   147ŌåÆ    r\"\\bplaceholder\\b\",\n   148ŌåÆ    r\"\\bscaffold(?:ing|ed)?\\b\",\n   149ŌåÆ    r\"\\btemporary\\b\",\n   150ŌåÆ    r\"\\bhardcoded\\b\",\n   151ŌåÆ    r\"\\bhardwired\\b\",\n   152ŌåÆ    r\"\\bno-?op\\b\",\n   153ŌåÆ    r\"\\bdummy\\b\",\n   154ŌåÆ    r\"\\bfake\\b\",\n   155ŌåÆ]\n   156ŌåÆ\n   157ŌåÆ# Terms that DISCHARGE an obligation (something fulfilled)\n   158ŌåÆDISCHARGE_TERMS = [\n   159ŌåÆ    r\"\\breplace\\b\",\n   160ŌåÆ    r\"\\bwire\\s+(?:up|in|into)\\b\",\n   161ŌåÆ    r\"\\bintegrat(?:e|ing|ed)\\b\",\n   162ŌåÆ    r\"\\bconnect\\b\",\n   163ŌåÆ    r\"\\bswap\\s+(?:out|in)\\b\",\n   164ŌåÆ    r\"\\bremove\\s+(?:mock|stub|placeholder|scaffold)\\b\",\n   165ŌåÆ    r\"\\bimplement\\s+real\\b\",\n   166ŌåÆ    r\"\\bfill\\s+in\\b\",\n   167ŌåÆ    r\"\\bcomplete\\s+(?:the\\s+)?(?:skeleton|scaffold)\\b\",\n   168ŌåÆ]\n   169ŌåÆ\n   170ŌåÆ# Compile patterns\n   171ŌåÆ_SCAFFOLD_RE = re.compile(\"|\".join(SCAFFOLD_TERMS), re.IGNORECASE)\n   172ŌåÆ_DISCHARGE_RE = re.compile(\"|\".join(DISCHARGE_TERMS), re.IGNORECASE)\n   173ŌåÆ\n   174ŌåÆ\n   175ŌåÆ@dataclass\n   176ŌåÆclass Obligation:\n   177ŌåÆ    \"\"\"A detected scaffolding obligation.\"\"\"\n   178ŌåÆ    phase: str           # e.g., \"Phase 2\", \"2.3\"\n   179ŌåÆ    term: str            # the matched scaffold term\n   180ŌåÆ    context: str         # surrounding sentence/line\n   181ŌåÆ    line_number: int\n   182ŌåÆ    discharged: bool     # True if a matching discharge was found in a later phase\n   183ŌåÆ    discharge_phase: str | None  # phase where discharge was found\n   184ŌåÆ    discharge_context: str | None\n   185ŌåÆ\n   186ŌåÆ\n   187ŌåÆ@dataclass\n   188ŌåÆclass ObligationReport:\n   189ŌåÆ    \"\"\"Result of obligation scanning.\"\"\"\n   190ŌåÆ    total_obligations: int\n   191ŌåÆ    discharged: int\n   192ŌåÆ    undischarged: int\n   193ŌåÆ    obligations: list[Obligation]\n   194ŌåÆ\n   195ŌåÆ    @property\n   196ŌåÆ    def has_undischarged(self) -> bool:\n   197ŌåÆ        return self.undischarged > 0\n   198ŌåÆ\n   199ŌåÆ\n   200ŌåÆdef scan_obligations(content: str) -> ObligationReport:\n   201ŌåÆ    \"\"\"Scan roadmap content for scaffolding obligations and discharge status.\n   202ŌåÆ\n   203ŌåÆ    Algorithm:\n   204ŌåÆ    1. Parse content into phase-delimited sections (by H2/H3 headings\n   205ŌåÆ       containing \"Phase\" or numbered sections).\n   206ŌåÆ    2. For each section, find all scaffold terms.\n   207ŌåÆ    3. For each scaffold term found, search ALL subsequent sections\n   208ŌåÆ       for a discharge term that references the same component.\n   209ŌåÆ    4. Report undischarged obligations.\n   210ŌåÆ\n   211ŌåÆ    Returns an ObligationReport with all findings.\n   212ŌåÆ    \"\"\"\n   213ŌåÆ    sections = _split_into_phases(content)\n   214ŌåÆ    obligations: list[Obligation] = []\n   215ŌåÆ\n   216ŌåÆ    for i, (phase_id, phase_content, start_line) in enumerate(sections):\n   217ŌåÆ        for match in _SCAFFOLD_RE.finditer(phase_content):\n   218ŌåÆ            term = match.group()\n   219ŌåÆ            context_line = _get_context_line(phase_content, match.start())\n   220ŌåÆ            abs_line = start_line + phase_content[:match.start()].count(\"\\n\")\n   221ŌåÆ\n   222ŌåÆ            # Extract the component name near the scaffold term\n   223ŌåÆ            component = _extract_component_context(phase_content, match.start())\n   224ŌåÆ\n   225ŌåÆ            # Search later phases for discharge\n   226ŌåÆ            discharged = False\n   227ŌåÆ            discharge_phase = None\n   228ŌåÆ            discharge_context = None\n   229ŌåÆ\n   230ŌåÆ            for j in range(i + 1, len(sections)):\n   231ŌåÆ                later_phase_id, later_content, _ = sections[j]\n   232ŌåÆ                # Look for discharge terms that reference the same component\n   233ŌåÆ                if _has_discharge(later_content, component):\n   234ŌåÆ                    discharged = True\n   235ŌåÆ                    discharge_phase = later_phase_id\n   236ŌåÆ                    discharge_match = _DISCHARGE_RE.search(later_content)\n   237ŌåÆ                    if discharge_match:\n   238ŌåÆ                        discharge_context = _get_context_line(\n   239ŌåÆ                            later_content, discharge_match.start()\n   240ŌåÆ                        )\n   241ŌåÆ                    break\n   242ŌåÆ\n   243ŌåÆ            obligations.append(Obligation(\n   244ŌåÆ                phase=phase_id,\n   245ŌåÆ                term=term,\n   246ŌåÆ                context=context_line,\n   247ŌåÆ                line_number=abs_line,\n   248ŌåÆ                discharged=discharged,\n   249ŌåÆ                discharge_phase=discharge_phase,\n   250ŌåÆ                discharge_context=discharge_context,\n   251ŌåÆ            ))\n   252ŌåÆ\n   253ŌåÆ    undischarged_count = sum(1 for o in obligations if not o.discharged)\n   254ŌåÆ    return ObligationReport(\n   255ŌåÆ        total_obligations=len(obligations),\n   256ŌåÆ        discharged=len(obligations) - undischarged_count,\n   257ŌåÆ        undischarged=undischarged_count,\n Anti-Instincts Gate -- Unified Specification\n\n<!-- Source: Merge (new content bridging V2+V5) -->\n\n> **Status**: Design Spec -- Ready for Implementation\n> **Created**: 2026-03-17\n> **Protocol**: sc:adversarial Step 5 (Merge Execution)\n> **Co-bases**: V2 (7.60) + V5 (7.55)\n> **Cherry-picks**: V4-2 (Fingerprints), V1-C (Spec Structural Audit), V1-D+V5-2 (Prompt Constraint)\n> **Target module**: `src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/`\n> **Pipeline latency added**: <1s (all checks are pure Python)\n> **LLM calls added**: 0\n\n---\n\n## 1. Problem Statement\n\n<!-- Source: Merge (new content bridging V2+V5) -->\n\nLLMs exhibit several correlated tendencies when generating multi-phase roadmaps from specifications. These tendencies cause systematic omission of integration wiring, undischarged scaffolding obligations, and dropped code-level requirements -- even when the output passes all existing format and fidelity gates.\n\nThe Anti-Instincts Gate is a unified deterministic defense layer that addresses four failure modes simultaneously:\n\n| Failure Mode | Detection Module | Source |\n|---|---|---|\n| Undischarged scaffolding (mocks/stubs never replaced) | `obligation_scanner.py` | V2-A |\n| Missing integration wiring (dispatch tables, registries never populated) | `integration_contracts.py` | V5-1 |\n| Code-level identifier omissions (function names, constants dropped) | `fingerprint.py` | V4-2 |\n| Extraction-stage requirement loss (upstream guard) | `spec_structural_audit.py` | V1-C |\n\nAdditionally, a prompt-level prevention layer reduces generation-time omissions:\n\n| Prevention Layer | Target | Source |\n|---|---|---|\n| Integration enumeration block in generate prompt | `prompts.py` | V1-D + V5-2 |\n| Integration wiring dimension in spec-fidelity prompt | `prompts.py` | V5-2 |\n\n---\n\n## 2. Evidence: The cli-portify Bug\n\n<!-- Source: Merge (new content bridging V2+V5) -->\n\n### What the spec defined\n\nThree release specs (v2.24, v2.24.1, v2.25) specified:\n\n- **Three-way dispatch**: `_run_programmatic_step()`, `_run_claude_step()`, `_run_convergence_step()`\n- **`PROGRAMMATIC_RUNNERS` dictionary**: Maps step IDs to Python functions\n- **Module dependency graph**: `executor.py --> steps/validate_config.py`, etc.\n- **Integration test**: `test_programmatic_step_routing`\n\n### What the roadmap produced\n\nThe roadmap reduced the executor to: \"Implement executor: sequential execution only, `--dry-run`, `--resume <step-id>`, signal handling\" with milestone M2: \"Sequential pipeline runs end-to-end with **mocked steps**.\"\n\nZero mentions of `PROGRAMMATIC_RUNNERS`, three-way dispatch, or the `executor.py --> steps/*.py` import chain.\n\n### How existing gates failed\n\nThe `SPEC_FIDELITY_GATE` enforces `high_severity_count == 0` deterministically, but the LLM generating the severity counts shared the same blindspot as the generator. The deterministic enforcement was sound; the LLM input to that gate was wrong.\n\n### How each module in this spec would have caught it\n\n| Module | Detection mechanism | Confidence |\n|---|---|---|\n| `obligation_scanner.py` | \"mocked steps\" in Phase 2 with no discharge in later phases | 85% |\n| `integration_contracts.py` | `PROGRAMMATIC_RUNNERS` dispatch pattern with no wiring task | 90% |\n| `fingerprint.py` | `_run_programmatic_step`, `PROGRAMMATIC_RUNNERS`, `test_programmatic_step_routing` absent from roadmap | 95% |\n| `spec_structural_audit.py` | Pseudocode block + `PROGRAMMATIC_RUNNERS` registry + `def _run_*` signatures inflate structural count beyond extraction's requirement count | 85% |\n\n---\n\n## 3. Architecture\n\n<!-- Source: Merge (new content bridging V2+V5) -->\n\n```\nSpec ŌöĆŌöĆ[V1-C: Structural audit]ŌöĆŌöĆ> Extraction validated\n                                         |\n                                    [V1-D+V5-2: Prompt constraint]\n                                         |\n                              LLM generates roadmap\n                                         |\n                                    Merge step\n                                         |\n                          +--------------+--------------+\n                          |              |              |\n                    [V2-A: Obligation    [V5-1: Contract   [V4-2: Fingerprint\n                     scanner]            extractor]         coverage]\n                          |              |              |\n                          +--------------+--------------+\n                                         |\n                              ANTI_INSTINCT_GATE (STRICT)\n                                         |\n                                    GATE FAIL / Proceed to spec-fidelity\n```\n\n**Pipeline position**: The three post-merge checks run as a single non-LLM step between `merge` and `test-strategy` in the pipeline. The structural audit runs between `extract` and `generate` as an executor-level hook.\n\n**Key design property**: All four detection modules are pure Python with zero LLM calls. This is deliberate -- LLM-on-LLM review shares the same blindspots that caused the original bug. The deterministic floor cannot be bypassed by completion bias.\n\n**Dual execution context**: When the roadmap pipeline executes within a sprint task context, gate results propagate to the sprint-level `TrailingGateRunner` and `TurnLedger` for economic tracking. In standalone mode, gate evaluation is synchronous pass/fail with no budget interaction. See Sections 9.5 and 16.5 for details.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Module 1: Obligation Scanner\n\n<!-- Source: V2-A (obligation scanner) -->\n\n### Concept\n\nA deterministic, regex-based post-generation pass that scans the merged roadmap for scaffolding terms and verifies each has a corresponding discharge task in a later phase. Catches the failure mode where early phases use \"mocked\", \"stub\", \"skeleton\", \"placeholder\" language that creates implicit obligations that later phases never fulfill.\n\n### Detection Axis\n\nV2-A's obligation scanner detects a fundamentally different failure mode than omission-based approaches. Rather than checking whether a requirement is present, it checks whether deferred commitments are fulfilled. This catches bugs where the requirement IS mentioned (as scaffolding) but the follow-through is missing.\n\n### Implementation\n\n**File**: `src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/obligation_scanner.py` (new, ~200 LOC)\n\n```python\n\"\"\"Obligation scanner -- detects undischarged scaffolding obligations in roadmaps.\n\nScans roadmap content for scaffolding terms (mock, stub, skeleton, placeholder,\nscaffold, temporary, hardcoded) that create implicit obligations, then verifies\neach obligation has a corresponding discharge term (replace, wire, integrate,\nconnect, implement real, remove mock, swap) in a later phase.\n\nPure function: content in, findings out. No I/O.\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom __future__ import annotations\n\nimport re\nfrom dataclasses import dataclass\n\n\n# --- Obligation vocabulary ---\n\n# Terms that CREATE an obligation (something deferred)\nSCAFFOLD_TERMS = [\n    r\"\\bmocked?\\b\",\n    r\"\\bstub(?:bed|s)?\\b\",\n    r\"\\bskeleton\\b\",\n    r\"\\bplaceholder\\b\",\n    r\"\\bscaffold(?:ing|ed)?\\b\",\n    r\"\\btemporary\\b\",\n    r\"\\bhardcoded\\b\",\n    r\"\\bhardwired\\b\",\n    r\"\\bno-?op\\b\",\n    r\"\\bdummy\\b\",\n    r\"\\bfake\\b\",\n]\n\n# Terms that DISCHARGE an obligation (something fulfilled)\nDISCHARGE_TERMS = [\n    r\"\\breplace\\b\",\n    r\"\\bwire\\s+(?:up|in|into)\\b\",\n    r\"\\bintegrat(?:e|ing|ed)\\b\",\n    r\"\\bconnect\\b\",\n    r\"\\bswap\\s+(?:out|in)\\b\",\n    r\"\\bremove\\s+(?:mock|stub|placeholder|scaffold)\\b\",\n    r\"\\bimplement\\s+real\\b\",\n    r\"\\bfill\\s+in\\b\",\n    r\"\\bcomplete\\s+(?:the\\s+)?(?:skeleton|scaffold)\\b\",\n]\n\n# Compile patterns\n_SCAFFOLD_RE = re.compile(\"|\".join(SCAFFOLD_TERMS), re.IGNORECASE)\n_DISCHARGE_RE = re.compile(\"|\".join(DISCHARGE_TERMS), re.IGNORECASE)\n\n\n@dataclass\nclass Obligation:\n    \"\"\"A detected scaffolding obligation.\"\"\"\n    phase: str           # e.g., \"Phase 2\", \"2.3\"\n    term: str            # the matched scaffold term\n    context: str         # surrounding sentence/line\n    line_number: int\n    discharged: bool     # True if a matching discharge was found in a later phase\n    discharge_phase: str | None  # phase where discharge was found\n    discharge_context: str | None\n\n\n@dataclass\nclass ObligationReport:\n    \"\"\"Result of obligation scanning.\"\"\"\n    total_obligations: int\n    discharged: int\n    undischarged: int\n    obligations: list[Obligation]\n\n    @property\n    def has_undischarged(self) -> bool:\n        return self.undischarged > 0\n\n\ndef scan_obligations(content: str) -> ObligationReport:\n    \"\"\"Scan roadmap content for scaffolding obligations and discharge status.\n\n    Algorithm:\n    1. Parse content into phase-delimited sections (by H2/H3 headings\n       containing \"Phase\" or numbered sections).\n    2. For each section, find all scaffold terms.\n    3. For each scaffold term found, search ALL subsequent sections\n       for a discharge term that references the same component.\n    4. Report undischarged obligations.\n\n    Returns an ObligationReport with all findings.\n    \"\"\"\n    sections = _split_into_phases(content)\n    obligations: list[Obligation] = []\n\n    for i, (phase_id, phase_content, start_line) in enumerate(sections):\n        for match in _SCAFFOLD_RE.finditer(phase_content):\n            term = match.group()\n            context_line = _get_context_line(phase_content, match.start())\n            abs_line = start_line + phase_content[:match.start()].count(\"\\n\")\n\n            # Extract the component name near the scaffold term\n            component = _extract_component_context(phase_content, match.start())\n\n            # Search later phases for discharge\n            discharged = False\n            discharge_phase = None\n            discharge_context = None\n\n            for j in range(i + 1, len(sections)):\n                later_phase_id, later_content, _ = sections[j]\n                # Look for discharge terms that reference the same component\n                if _has_discharge(later_content, component):\n                    discharged = True\n                    discharge_phase = later_phase_id\n                    discharge_match = _DISCHARGE_RE.search(later_content)\n                    if discharge_match:\n                        discharge_context = _get_context_line(\n                            later_content, discharge_match.start()\n                        )\n                    break\n\n            obligations.append(Obligation(\n                phase=phase_id,\n                term=term,\n                context=context_line,\n                line_number=abs_line,\n                discharged=discharged,\n                discharge_phase=discharge_phase,\n                discharge_context=discharge_context,\n            ))\n\n    undischarged_count = sum(1 for o in obligations if not o.discharged)\n    return ObligationReport(\n        total_obligations=len(obligations),\n        discharged=len(obligations) - undischarged_count,\n        undischarged=undischarged_count,\n        obligations=obligations,\n    )\n\n\ndef _split_into_phases(content: str) -> list[tuple[str, str, int]]:\n    \"\"\"Split content into (phase_id, text, start_line_number) tuples.\n\n    Splits on H2/H3 headings that contain phase-like patterns:\n    \"## Phase 2\", \"### 2.3 Executor\", \"## Step 4\", etc.\n    \"\"\"\n    phase_pattern = re.compile(\n        r\"^(#{2,3})\\s+((?:Phase|Step|Stage|Milestone)\\s+\\d+[\\w.]*.*?)$\",\n        re.MULTILINE | re.IGNORECASE,\n    )\n    matches = list(phase_pattern.finditer(content))\n    if not matches:\n        # Fallback: treat whole content as one section\n        return [(\"entire-document\", content, 1)]\n\n    sections: list[tuple[str, str, int]] = []\n    for i, m in enumerate(matches):\n        phase_id = m.group(2).strip()\n        start = m.end()\n        end = matches[i + 1].start() if i + 1 < len(matches) else len(content)\n        start_line = content[:m.start()].count(\"\\n\") + 1\n        sections.append((phase_id, content[start:end], start_line))\n\n    return sections\n\n\ndef _get_context_line(text: str, pos: int) -> str:\n    \"\"\"Extract the line containing position `pos`.\"\"\"\n    start = text.rfind(\"\\n\", 0, pos) + 1\n    end = text.find(\"\\n\", pos)\n    if end == -1:\n        end = len(text)\n    return text[start:end].strip()\n\n\ndef _extract_component_context(text: str, pos: int) -> str:\n    \"\"\"Extract likely component name near a scaffold term.\n\n    Looks for capitalized words, quoted terms, or code-formatted","numLines":300,"startLine":1,"totalLines":1694}}}

This reduces false positives from \"the test uses mocks\" because test description scaffold terms will not share component context with phase milestone scaffold terms.\n   357ŌåÆ- Scaffold terms inside code blocks (backtick-fenced) are treated as potential false positives and flagged at MEDIUM severity rather than failing the gate.\n   358ŌåÆ- An `# obligation-exempt` comment mechanism is available for legitimate scaffolding strategies where mocks ARE the final implementation (e.g., test doubles).\n   359ŌåÆ- Phase 1 enforcement: STRICT on undischarged obligations, with the component-context filter active.\n   360ŌåÆ\n   361ŌåÆ---\n   362ŌåÆ\n   363ŌåÆ## 5. Module 2: Integration Contract Extractor\n   364ŌåÆ\n   365ŌåÆ<!-- Source: V5-1 (integration contract extractor) -->\n   366ŌåÆ\n   367ŌåÆ### Concept\n   368ŌåÆ\n   369ŌåÆA deterministic pre-validation step that extracts \"integration contracts\" from the spec and verifies each has a corresponding explicit task in the roadmap. An integration contract is any place where a data structure maps identifiers to callables, a constructor accepts injectable dependencies, an explicit wiring step is described, or a lookup/dispatch mechanism is defined.\n   370ŌåÆ\n   371ŌåÆ### Detection Axis\n   372ŌåÆ\n   373ŌåÆV5-1 is mechanism-aware. It does not just detect missing identifiers but verifies the roadmap contains explicit wiring tasks for specific integration mechanisms. The key insight: \"implementing components\" is necessary but not sufficient. The wiring task itself must be explicit. Building a class does not register it in a dispatch table.\n   374ŌåÆ\n   375ŌåÆ### Implementation\n   376ŌåÆ\n   377ŌåÆ**File**: `src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/integration_contracts.py` (new, ~250 LOC)\n   378ŌåÆ\n   379ŌåÆ```python\n   380ŌåÆ\"\"\"Integration contract extraction and verification.\n   381ŌåÆ\n   382ŌåÆExtracts non-obvious integration points from spec text and verifies\n   383ŌåÆeach has an explicit corresponding task in the roadmap. Catches the\n   384ŌåÆ\"pattern-matching trap\" where LLMs assume standard skeleton->implement\n   385ŌåÆphasing covers custom dispatch/wiring mechanisms.\n   386ŌåÆ\"\"\"\n   387ŌåÆ\n   388ŌåÆfrom __future__ import annotations\n   389ŌåÆ\n   390ŌåÆimport re\n   391ŌåÆfrom dataclasses import dataclass, field\n   392ŌåÆ\n   393ŌåÆ\n   394ŌåÆ# --- Pattern definitions for integration contract detection ---\n   395ŌåÆ# Expanded to cover all 7 categories from the integration mechanism taxonomy.\n   396ŌåÆ\n   397ŌåÆDISPATCH_PATTERNS = [\n   398ŌåÆ    # Category 1: Dict dispatch tables\n   399ŌåÆ    re.compile(\n   400ŌåÆ        r'\\b(?:dispatch[_\\s]?table|RUNNERS|_RUNNERS|HANDLERS|'\n   401ŌåÆ        r'DISPATCH|routing[_\\s]?table|command[_\\s]?map|step[_\\s]?map|'\n   402ŌåÆ        r'plugin[_\\s]?registry)\\b',\n   403ŌåÆ        re.IGNORECASE,\n   404ŌåÆ    ),\n   405ŌåÆ    # Category 2: Plugin registry / explicit wiring\n   406ŌåÆ    re.compile(\n   407ŌåÆ        r'\\b(?:populate|register|wire|inject|bind|map|route)\\s+'\n   408ŌåÆ        r'(?:the\\s+|all\\s+|each\\s+)?'\n   409ŌåÆ        r'(?:implementations?|runners?|handlers?|plugins?|steps?|commands?)\\b',\n   410ŌåÆ        re.IGNORECASE,\n   411ŌåÆ    ),\n   412ŌåÆ    # Category 3: Callback injection / constructor injection\n   413ŌåÆ    re.compile(\n   414ŌåÆ        r'\\b(?:accepts?|takes?|requires?|expects?)\\s+(?:a\\s+)?'\n   415ŌåÆ        r'(?:Callable|Protocol|ABC|Interface|Factory|Provider|Registry)\\b',\n   416ŌåÆ        re.IGNORECASE,\n   417ŌåÆ    ),\n   418ŌåÆ    # Category 3 (continued): Type annotations for dispatch\n   419ŌåÆ    re.compile(\n   420ŌåÆ        r'\\b(?:Dict|Mapping|dict)\\s*\\[\\s*str\\s*,\\s*(?:Callable|Awaitable|Coroutine)\\b',\n   421ŌåÆ        re.IGNORECASE,\n   422ŌåÆ    ),\n   423ŌåÆ    # Module 3: Fingerprint Extraction\n   674ŌåÆ\n   675ŌåÆ<!-- Source: V4-2 (fingerprint extraction) -->\n   676ŌåÆ\n   677ŌåÆ### Concept\n   678ŌåÆ\n   679ŌåÆGoes beyond formal requirement IDs to extract \"structural fingerprints\" -- function names, class names, data structure names, and design pattern names that appear in code fences or backtick-delimited spans in the spec. Verifies each fingerprint appears in the roadmap. This is mechanism-agnostic: it catches any code-level identifier omission regardless of whether the spec uses FR-NNN tags or specific integration patterns.\n   680ŌåÆ\n   681ŌåÆ### Detection Axis\n   682ŌåÆ\n   683ŌåÆV4-2 has the highest single-check efficacy (95% confidence) because it operates on the exact code-level identifiers that specs contain. A spec that mentions `_run_programmatic_step` in backticks expects the roadmap to plan for that function. If the roadmap does not mention it at all, coverage is objectively incomplete.\n   684ŌåÆ\n   685ŌåÆ### Implementation\n   686ŌåÆ\n   687ŌåÆ**File**: `src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/fingerprint.py` (new, ~150 LOC)\n   688ŌåÆ\n   689ŌåÆ```python\n   690ŌåÆ\"\"\"Structural fingerprint extraction and coverage checking.\n   691ŌåÆ\n   692ŌåÆExtracts code-level identifiers from spec content (backtick-delimited names,\n   693ŌåÆcode-block definitions, ALL_CAPS constants) and verifies a minimum coverage\n   694ŌåÆratio appears in the roadmap. Catches wholesale omission of design detail\n   695ŌåÆthat text-matching on formal IDs would miss.\n   696ŌåÆ\n   697ŌåÆPure function: content in, result out. No I/O.\n   698ŌåÆ\"\"\"\n   699ŌåÆ"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"c4f6d05a-351f-4ddd-8de8-7556feb4a198","uuid":"6907d8a7-e1f4-4a51-a411-3b92c861d10c","timestamp":"2026-03-20T17:48:28.787Z","tool_use_result":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"/config/workspace/IronClaude/.dev/releases/current/v3.1_Anti-instincts__/anti-instincts-gate-unified.md","content":"    Looks for capitalized words, quoted terms, or code-formatted\n    terms within ~60 chars of the match position.\n    \"\"\"\n    window_start = max(0, pos - 60)\n    window_end = min(len(text), pos + 60)\n    window = text[window_start:window_end]\n\n    # Try to find backtick-delimited terms first\n    code_terms = re.findall(r\"`([^`]+)`\", window)\n    if code_terms:\n        return code_terms[0].lower()\n\n    # Try capitalized multi-word terms (e.g., \"Executor Skeleton\")\n    cap_terms = re.findall(r\"[A-Z][a-z]+(?:\\s+[A-Z][a-z]+)*\", window)\n    if cap_terms:\n        return cap_terms[0].lower()\n\n    # Fallback: the whole line context\n    return _get_context_line(text, pos).lower()\n\n\ndef _has_discharge(content: str, component: str) -> bool:\n    \"\"\"Check if content contains a discharge term referencing the component.\"\"\"\n    if not component:\n        # No component context -- just check for any discharge term\n        return bool(_DISCHARGE_RE.search(content))\n\n    # Check if content mentions both a discharge term AND the component\n    has_discharge = bool(_DISCHARGE_RE.search(content))\n    has_component = component.lower() in content.lower()\n    return has_discharge and has_component\n```\n\n### Vocabulary Management\n\n<!-- Source: V2-A (obligation scanner) -->\n\nThe scaffold and discharge term lists are the critical data. Each scaffold term has at least one known discharge pairing:\n\n| Scaffold Term | Expected Discharge Terms |\n|---|---|\n| mock/mocked | replace mock, remove mock, swap out mock |\n| stub/stubbed | replace stub, implement real, fill in |\n| skeleton | complete skeleton, flesh out, fill in |\n| placeholder | replace placeholder, implement real |\n| scaffold/scaffolding | remove scaffolding, replace scaffold |\n| temporary | replace temporary, make permanent |\n| hardcoded | make configurable, parameterize, replace hardcoded |\n| no-op | implement, add logic, replace no-op |\n| dummy | replace dummy, implement real |\n| fake | replace fake, use real |\n\n### False Positive Mitigation\n\n<!-- Source: V2-A (obligation scanner), adapted per refactor-plan Section 6 Weakness 1 -->\n\n- Component context extraction uses a 60-char window to associate scaffold terms with nearby component names. This reduces false positives from \"the test uses mocks\" because test description scaffold terms will not share component context with phase milestone scaffold terms.\n- Scaffold terms inside code blocks (backtick-fenced) are treated as potential false positives and flagged at MEDIUM severity rather than failing the gate.\n- An `# obligation-exempt` comment mechanism is available for legitimate scaffolding strategies where mocks ARE the final implementation (e.g., test doubles).\n- Phase 1 enforcement: STRICT on undischarged obligations, with the component-context filter active.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Module 2: Integration Contract Extractor\n\n<!-- Source: V5-1 (integration contract extractor) -->\n\n### Concept\n\nA deterministic pre-validation step that extracts \"integration contracts\" from the spec and verifies each has a corresponding explicit task in the roadmap. An integration contract is any place where a data structure maps identifiers to callables, a constructor accepts injectable dependencies, an explicit wiring step is described, or a lookup/dispatch mechanism is defined.\n\n### Detection Axis\n\nV5-1 is mechanism-aware. It does not just detect missing identifiers but verifies the roadmap contains explicit wiring tasks for specific integration mechanisms. The key insight: \"implementing components\" is necessary but not sufficient. The wiring task itself must be explicit. Building a class does not register it in a dispatch table.\n\n### Implementation\n\n**File**: `src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/integration_contracts.py` (new, ~250 LOC)\n\n```python\n\"\"\"Integration contract extraction and verification.\n\nExtracts non-obvious integration points from spec text and verifies\neach has an explicit corresponding task in the roadmap. Catches the\n\"pattern-matching trap\" where LLMs assume standard skeleton->implement\nphasing covers custom dispatch/wiring mechanisms.\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom __future__ import annotations\n\nimport re\nfrom dataclasses import dataclass, field\n\n\n# --- Pattern definitions for integration contract detection ---\n# Expanded to cover all 7 categories from the integration mechanism taxonomy.\n\nDISPATCH_PATTERNS = [\n    # Category 1: Dict dispatch tables\n    re.compile(\n        r'\\b(?:dispatch[_\\s]?table|RUNNERS|_RUNNERS|HANDLERS|'\n        r'DISPATCH|routing[_\\s]?table|command[_\\s]?map|step[_\\s]?map|'\n        r'plugin[_\\s]?registry)\\b',\n        re.IGNORECASE,\n    ),\n    # Category 2: Plugin registry / explicit wiring\n    re.compile(\n        r'\\b(?:populate|register|wire|inject|bind|map|route)\\s+'\n        r'(?:the\\s+|all\\s+|each\\s+)?'\n        r'(?:implementations?|runners?|handlers?|plugins?|steps?|commands?)\\b',\n        re.IGNORECASE,\n    ),\n    # Category 3: Callback injection / constructor injection\n    re.compile(\n        r'\\b(?:accepts?|takes?|requires?|expects?)\\s+(?:a\\s+)?'\n        r'(?:Callable|Protocol|ABC|Interface|Factory|Provider|Registry)\\b',\n        re.IGNORECASE,\n    ),\n    # Category 3 (continued): Type annotations for dispatch\n    re.compile(\n        r'\\b(?:Dict|Mapping|dict)\\s*\\[\\s*str\\s*,\\s*(?:Callable|Awaitable|Coroutine)\\b',\n        re.IGNORECASE,\n    ),\n    # Category 4: Strategy pattern\n    re.compile(\n        r'\\b(?:Context\\s*\\(\\s*strategy\\s*=|Strategy|ConcreteStrategy|'\n        r'set_strategy|get_strategy)\\b',\n        re.IGNORECASE,\n    ),\n    # Category 5: Middleware chain\n    re.compile(\n        r'\\b(?:middleware|app\\.use|pipeline\\.add|add_middleware|'\n        r'use_middleware)\\b',\n        re.IGNORECASE,\n    ),\n    # Category 6: Event binding\n    re.compile(\n        r'\\b(?:emitter\\.on|addEventListener|subscribe|on_event|'\n        r'event_handler|add_listener)\\b',\n        re.IGNORECASE,\n    ),\n    # Category 7: DI container\n    re.compile(\n        r'\\b(?:container\\.bind|container\\.register|Provider|'\n        r'Injector|inject_dependency|DependencyContainer)\\b',\n        re.IGNORECASE,\n    ),\n]\n\n# Patterns that indicate a roadmap task explicitly addresses wiring\nWIRING_TASK_PATTERNS = [\n    # Explicit creation/population of dispatch/registry mechanisms\n    re.compile(\n        r'\\b(?:create|build|construct|populate|wire|assemble|register)\\s+'\n        r'(?:the\\s+|a\\s+)?'\n        r'(?:dispatch|routing|registry|runner|handler|command|middleware|'\n        r'event|strategy|plugin)\\s*'\n        r'(?:table|map|dict|registry|lookup|chain|binding|container)\\b',\n        re.IGNORECASE,\n    ),\n    # Explicit wiring of implementations into mechanisms\n    re.compile(\n        r'\\b(?:wire|connect|bind|inject|register|plug)\\s+.*?'\n        r'(?:implementations?|runners?|handlers?|plugins?|strategies?|'\n        r'middlewares?|listeners?)\\s+'\n        r'(?:into|to|with|in)\\b',\n        re.IGNORECASE,\n    ),\n    # Specific named mechanisms from common specs\n    re.compile(\n        r'\\bPROGRAMMATIC_RUNNERS\\b|\\bDISPATCH_TABLE\\b|\\bHANDLER_REGISTRY\\b|'\n        r'\\bMIDDLEWARE_CHAIN\\b|\\bEVENT_BINDINGS\\b|\\bROUTE_MAP\\b',\n    ),\n    # Strategy/middleware/event-specific wiring verbs\n    re.compile(\n        r'\\b(?:configure|set[_\\s]up|initialize|bootstrap)\\s+'\n        r'(?:the\\s+)?'\n        r'(?:strategy|middleware|event\\s+binding|DI\\s+container|'\n        r'dependency\\s+injection|plugin\\s+registry)\\b',\n        re.IGNORECASE,\n    ),\n]\n\n\n@dataclass\nclass IntegrationContract:\n    \"\"\"A single integration point extracted from a spec.\"\"\"\n    id: str                          # IC-001, IC-002, ...\n    mechanism: str                   # \"dispatch_table\", \"registry\", \"injection\", etc.\n    spec_evidence: str               # verbatim quote from spec\n    spec_location: str               # line number or section heading\n    description: str                 # human-readable description\n    requires_explicit_wiring: bool   # True if cannot be implicit\n\n\n@dataclass\nclass WiringCoverage:\n    \"\"\"Result of checking whether a contract is covered by roadmap tasks.\"\"\"\n    contract: IntegrationContract\n    covered: bool\n    roadmap_evidence: str            # (\"dispatch\", \"runner\", \"handler\", \"command_map\", \"step_map\")):\n        return \"dispatch_table\"\n    if \"registry\" in lower or \"register\" in lower:\n        return \"registry\"\n    if any(k in lower for k in (\"inject\", \"callable\", \"protocol\", \"factory\", \"provider\")):\n        return \"dependency_injection\"\n    if any(k in lower for k in (\"wire\", \"bind\", \"populate\")):\n        return \"explicit_wiring\"\n    if any(k in lower for k in (\"route\", \"routing\")):\n        return \"routing\"\n    if any(k in lower for k in (\"strategy\", \"concretestrategy\")):\n        return \"strategy_pattern\"\n    if any(k in lower for k in (\"middleware\", \"app.use\", \"pipeline.add\")):\n        return \"middleware_chain\"\n    if any(k in lower for k in (\"emitter\", \"addeventlistener\", \"subscribe\", \"listener\")):\n        return \"event_binding\"\n    if any(k in lower for k in (\"container\", \"injector\", re.findall(r'\\b[A-Z][a-z]+(?:[A-Z][a-z]+)+\\b', text)\n    return upper_snake + pascal\n```\n\n### Pattern Library Expansion\n\n<!-- Source: V5-1 (integration contract extractor), adapted per refactor-plan Section 6 Weakness 2 -->\n\nThe `DISPATCH_PATTERNS` and `WIRING_TASK_PATTERNS` have been expanded beyond V5's original 4+3 patterns to cover all 7 categories from V5's integration mechanism taxonomy:\n\n| Category | DISPATCH_PATTERNS coverage | WIRING_TASK_PATTERNS coverage |\n|---|---|---|\n| Dict dispatch | `DISPATCH_TABLE`, `RUNNERS`, `HANDLERS`, `command_map`, `step_map` | Module 3: Fingerprint Extraction\n\n<!-- Source: V4-2 (fingerprint extraction) -->\n\n### Concept\n\nGoes beyond formal requirement IDs to extract \"structural fingerprints\" -- function names, class names, data structure names, and design pattern names that appear in code fences or backtick-delimited spans in the spec. Verifies each fingerprint appears in the roadmap. This is mechanism-agnostic: it catches any code-level identifier omission regardless of whether the spec uses FR-NNN tags or specific integration patterns.\n\n### Detection Axis\n\nV4-2 has the highest single-check efficacy (95% confidence) because it operates on the exact code-level identifiers that specs contain. A spec that mentions `_run_programmatic_step` in backticks expects the roadmap to plan for that function. The V5-1 contract extractor provides the verb-anchored check that distinguishes mention from planning.\n   821ŌåÆ\n   822ŌåÆ---\n   823ŌåÆ\n   824ŌåÆ## 7. Module 4: Spec Structural Audit\n   825ŌåÆ\n   826ŌåÆ<!-- Source: V1-C (spec structural audit) -->\n   827ŌåÆ\n   828ŌåÆ### Concept\n   829ŌåÆ\n   830ŌåÆA deterministic upstream guard between the spec input and the extraction output. It catches the case where the extraction LLM itself drops requirements before they ever reach the roadmap. Neither the obligation scanner, contract extractor, nor fingerprint check can detect this -- all downstream checks are vacuous if extraction drops a requirement.\n   831ŌåÆ\n   832ŌåÆ### Detection Axis\n   833ŌåÆ\n   834ŌåÆV1-C is the only solution that guards the extraction step itself. Backtick-delimited identifiers: `_run_programmatic_step()`\n    2. Code-fenced blocks: function/class definitions\n    3. ALL_CAPS constants (likely important data structures)\n    \"\"\"\n    fingerprints: list[Fingerprint] = []\n\n    # 1. Backtick identifiers (most reliable)\n    for match in re.finditer(r'`([a-zA-Z_]\\w*(?:\\(\\))?)`', content):\n        text = match.group(1).rstrip('()')\n        if len(text) >= 4:  # skip trivial identifiers\n            ctx_start = max(0, match.start() - 40)\n            ctx_end = min(len(content), match.end() + 40)\n            fingerprints.append(Fingerprint(\n                text=text,\n                category=\"identifier\",\n                source_context=content[ctx_start:ctx_end].replace('\\n', ' '),\n            ))\n\n    # 2. Code block function/class definitions\n    code_block_pat = re.compile(r'```(?:python)?\\n(.*?)```', re.DOTALL)\n    for block_match in code_block_pat.finditer(content):\n        block = block_match.group(1)\n        for def_match in re.finditer(r'(?:def|class)\\s+(\\w+)', block):\n            fingerprints.append(Fingerprint(\n                text=def_match.group(1),\n                category=\"definition\",\n                source_context=def_match.group(0),\n            ))\n\n    # 3. ALL_CAPS constants (likely important data structures)\n    for match in re.finditer(r'\\b([A-Z][A-Z_]{3,})\\b', content):\n        text = match.group(1)\n        if text not in _EXCLUDED_CONSTANTS:\n            fingerprints.append(Fingerprint(\n                text=text,\n                category=\"constant\",\n                source_context=content[\n                    max(0, match.start() - 40):match.end() + 40\n                ].replace('\\n', ' '),\n            ))\n\n    # Deduplicate by text\n    seen: set[str] = set()\n    unique: list[Fingerprint] = []\n    for fp in fingerprints:\n        if fp.text not in seen:\n            seen.add(fp.text)\n            unique.append(fp)\n\n    return unique\n\n\ndef check_fingerprint_coverage(\n    spec_content: str,\n    roadmap_content: str,\n    min_coverage_ratio: float = 0.7,\n) -> tuple[bool, float, list[Fingerprint], list[Fingerprint]]:\n    \"\"\"Check that spec fingerprints appear in roadmap.\n\n    Returns (passed, coverage_ratio, all_fingerprints, missing_fingerprints).\n    Gate passes if coverage ratio >= min_coverage_ratio.\n\n    The ratio threshold (default 0.7) accounts for the fact that not every\n    backtick identifier in a spec is a hard requirement -- some are examples,\n    alternatives, or references to existing code. But a coverage ratio below\n    70% strongly indicates wholesale omission of design detail.\n    \"\"\"\n    spec_fps = extract_code_fingerprints(spec_content)\n    if not spec_fps:\n        return True, 1.0, [], []\n\n    roadmap_lower = roadmap_content.lower()\n    missing: list[Fingerprint] = []\n    for fp in spec_fps:\n        if fp.text.lower() not in roadmap_lower:\n            missing.append(fp)\n\n    coverage = 1.0 - (len(missing) / len(spec_fps))\n    return coverage >= min_coverage_ratio, coverage, spec_fps, missing\n```\n\n### Threshold Rationale\n\n<!-- Source: V4-2 (fingerprint extraction), adapted per refactor-plan Section 6 Weakness 4 -->\n\nThe default `min_coverage_ratio` of 0.7 is conservative because:\n- Not every backtick identifier is a requirement (some are examples, alternatives, or references).\n- A single mention in a design overview adds 1 to the numerator but does not inflate the ratio enough to mask wholesale omissions.\n- The 0.7 threshold means 30% of spec identifiers can be absent before the gate triggers, accommodating illustrative content.\n- Empirical tuning is expected: shadow-mode runs on real pipelines will calibrate the final value.\n\n### Interaction with A-009 (\"Mentioned is not Planned\")\n\nThe fingerprint check is presence-based and therefore susceptible to the \"mentioned is not planned\" limitation (diff analysis A-009). However, the 0.7 threshold is for coverage ratio, not exact-match. A roadmap that passively mentions identifiers without planning tasks for them would still need to mention 70%+ of spec fingerprints to pass, which in practice requires genuine engagement with the spec content. The V5-1 contract extractor provides the verb-anchored check that distinguishes mention from planning.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Module 4: Spec Structural Audit\n\n<!-- Source: V1-C (spec structural audit) -->\n\n### Concept\n\nA deterministic upstream guard between the spec input and the extraction output. It catches the case where the extraction LLM itself drops requirements before they ever reach the roadmap. Neither the obligation scanner, contract extractor, nor fingerprint check can detect this -- all downstream checks are vacuous if extraction drops a requirement.\n\n### Detection Axis\n\nV1-C is the only solution that guards the extraction step itself. All other checks assume the extraction is correct and validate downstream artifacts. If the extraction LLM drops the dispatch requirement entirely, V2-A has nothing to scan, V5-1 has nothing to extract contracts from, and V4-2 has no fingerprints to compare against.\n\n### Implementation\n\n**File**: `src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/spec_structural_audit.py` (new, ~80 LOC)\n\n```python\n\"\"\"Spec structural audit -- upstream guard on extraction quality.\n\nCounts structural requirement indicators in the raw spec (code blocks,\nMUST/SHALL clauses, function signatures, test names, registry patterns)\nand compares against the extraction's total_requirements frontmatter value.\nIf the extraction reports suspiciously few requirements relative to the\nspec's structural richness, it flags a potential extraction failure.\n\nPure function: spec text + extraction requirement count in, result out.\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom __future__ import annotations\n\nimport re\nfrom dataclasses import dataclass\n\n\n@dataclass\nclass SpecStructuralAudit:\n    \"\"\"Result of structural indicator counting.\"\"\"\n    code_block_count: int          # Number of code blocks in spec\n    must_shall_count: int          # Sentences with MUST/SHALL/REQUIRED\n    function_signature_count: int  # def foo() patterns in code blocks\n    class_definition_count: int    # class Foo patterns in code blocks\n    test_name_count: int           # test_* patterns\n    registry_pattern_count: int    # UPPERCASE_DICT = { patterns\n    pseudocode_blocks: int         # Blocks showing control flow (if/else/for)\n    total_structural_indicators: int\n\n\ndef audit_spec_structure(spec_text: str) -> SpecStructuralAudit:\n    \"\"\"Count structural requirement indicators in the raw spec.\n\n    These indicators approximate the spec's \"requirement density.\" A spec\n    with many code blocks, function signatures, MUST clauses, and test names\n    should produce a correspondingly rich extraction. If the extraction's\n    total_requirements is far below the indicator count, the extraction may\n    have dropped requirements.\n    \"\"\"\n    code_blocks = re.findall(r\"```[\\s\\S]*?```\", spec_text)\n    code_text = \"\\n\".join(code_blocks)\n\n    code_block_count = len(code_blocks)\n    must_shall_count = len(re.findall(\n        r\"\\b(?:MUST|SHALL|REQUIRED)\\b\", spec_text\n    ))\n    function_signature_count = len(re.findall(\n        r\"\\bdef\\s+\\w+\\s*\\(\", code_text\n    ))\n    class_definition_count = len(re.findall(\n        r\"\\bclass\\s+\\w+\", code_text\n    ))\n    test_name_count = len(re.findall(\n        r\"\\btest_\\w+\", spec_text\n    ))\n    registry_pattern_count = len(re.findall(\n        r\"\\b[A-Z][A-Z_]+\\s*=\\s*\\{\", code_text","numLines":200,"startLine":698,"totalLines":1694}}}

If a scaffold term (e.g., \"mocked\") appears on a line ending with `# obligation-exempt`, that specific obligation is excluded from the undischarged count. Multi-line exemptions require the comment on each line.\n\n**API Impact on `obligation_scanner.py`**:\n- `scan_obligations()` must check each line containing a scaffold match for a trailing `# obligation-exempt` comment.\n- Exempt obligations are still recorded in the `Obligation` dataclass but with an `exempt=True` field (or equivalent filtering).\n- `ObligationReport.undischarged_count` excludes exempt obligations.\n\n---\n\n## OQ-004: MEDIUM Severity vs STRICT Gate Blocking\n\n**Decision**: Separate `medium_severity_obligations` frontmatter field, excluded from gate blocking.\n\n**Resolution**: Scaffold terms found inside code blocks (backtick-fenced) are demoted to MEDIUM severity. MEDIUM severity obligations are stored in a separate frontmatter field (`medium_severity_obligations`) and are NOT counted toward the `undischarged_obligations` field that the ANTI_INSTINCT_GATE checks. The gate blocks only on HIGH severity (non-code-block) undischarged obligations.\n\n**API Impact on `obligation_scanner.py`**:\n- `Obligation` dataclass includes a `severity` field: `\"HIGH\"` (default) or `\"MEDIUM\"` (code-block context).\n- `ObligationReport` exposes `undischarged_count` property that returns count where `discharged=False AND severity != \"MEDIUM\"`.\n- Code-block detection: scaffold terms within ``` fenced blocks are tagged MEDIUM.\n\n---\n\n## OQ-005: D-03/D-04 Coexistence (Defense-in-Depth)\n\n**Decision**: Both gates evaluate independently per NFR-010.\n\n**Resolution**: The existing `WIRING_GATE` (D-03) and the new `ANTI_INSTINCT_GATE` (D-04) operate as independent pipeline gates. Both evaluate on every run. Neither short-circuits the other. If either fails, the pipeline halts. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-opus-4-6","id":"msg_01QcPJUBwkTziJZgitTmvbCJ","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01X3ETR3WirjNBAEqARD83s5","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/config/workspace/IronClaude/src/superclaude/cli/roadmap/obligation_scanner.py","content":"\"\"\"Obligation scanner -- detects undischarged scaffolding obligations in roadmaps.\n\nScans roadmap content for scaffolding terms (mock, stub, skeleton, placeholder,\nscaffold, temporary, hardcoded) that create implicit obligations, then verifies\neach obligation has a corresponding discharge term (replace, wire, integrate,\nconnect, implement real, remove mock, swap) in a later phase.\n\nPure function: content in, findings out. No I/O.\n\nImplements FR-MOD1.1 through FR-MOD1.8.\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom __future__ import annotations\n\nimport re\nfrom dataclasses import dataclass\n\n\n# --- FR-MOD1.1: Obligation vocabulary (11 scaffold terms) ---\n\nSCAFFOLD_TERMS = [\n    r\"\\bmocked?\\b\",\n    r\"\\bstub(?:bed|s)?\\b\",\n    r\"\\bskeleton\\b\",\n    r\"\\bplaceholder\\b\",\n    r\"\\bscaffold(?:ing|ed)?\\b\",\n    r\"\\btemporary\\b\",\n    r\"\\bhardcoded\\b\",\n    r\"\\bhardwired\\b\",\n    r\"\\bno-?op\\b\",\n    r\"\\bdummy\\b\",\n    r\"\\bfake\\b\",\n]\n\n# Terms that DISCHARGE an obligation (something fulfilled)\nDISCHARGE_TERMS = [\n    r\"\\breplace\\b\",\n    r\"\\bwire\\s+(?:up|in|into)\\b\",\n    r\"\\bintegrat(?:e|ing|ed)\\b\",\n    r\"\\bconnect\\b\",\n    r\"\\bswap\\s+(?:out|in)\\b\",\n    r\"\\bremove\\s+(?:mock|stub|placeholder|scaffold)\\b\",\n    r\"\\bimplement\\s+real\\b\",\n    r\"\\bfill\\s+in\\b\",\n    r\"\\bcomplete\\s+(?:the\\s+)?(?:skeleton|scaffold)\\b\",\n]\n\n# Compile patterns\n_SCAFFOLD_RE = re.compile(\"|\".join(SCAFFOLD_TERMS), re.IGNORECASE)\n_DISCHARGE_RE = re.compile(\"|\".join(DISCHARGE_TERMS), re.IGNORECASE)\n\n# FR-MOD1.7: Exempt comment pattern (OQ-003 resolution: per-line scope)\n_EXEMPT_COMMENT_RE = re.compile(r\"#\\s*obligation-exempt\", re.IGNORECASE)\n\n# FR-MOD1.8: Code block detection for severity demotion (OQ-004 resolution)\n_CODE_BLOCK_RE = re.compile(r\"```[\\s\\S]*?```\")\n\n\n# --- FR-MOD1.6: Dataclasses ---\n\n\n@dataclass\nclass Obligation:\n    \"\"\"A detected scaffolding obligation.\"\"\"\n\n    phase: str  # e.g., \"Phase 2\", \"2.3\"\n    term: str  # the matched scaffold term\n    component: str  # nearby component context\n    context: str  # surrounding sentence/line\n    line_number: int\n    severity: str  # \"HIGH\" or \"MEDIUM\" (FR-MOD1.8)\n    discharged: bool  # True if a matching discharge was found in a later phase\n    exempt: bool  # True if line has # obligation-exempt (FR-MOD1.7)\n    discharge_phase: str | None  # Parse content into phase-delimited sections (FR-MOD1.2: H2/H3 fallback).\n    2. For each section, find all scaffold terms (FR-MOD1.1).\n    3. discharge_context = None\n\n            for j in range(i + 1, len(sections)):\n                later_phase_id, later_content, _ = sections[j]\n                # FR-MOD1.5: Dual-condition discharge list(fallback_pattern.finditer(content))\n\n    if not matches:\n        # Final fallback: treat whole content as one section\n        return [(\"entire-document\", content, 1)]\n\n    sections:
